\hypertarget{interfaceArrayRemove__mod_1_1genRemoved}{}\doxysection{Array\+Remove\+\_\+mod\+::gen\+Removed Interface Reference}
\label{interfaceArrayRemove__mod_1_1genRemoved}\index{ArrayRemove\_mod::genRemoved@{ArrayRemove\_mod::genRemoved}}


Generate and return an allocatable array containing the remaining parts of the input array as a sequence after removing the input {\ttfamily Pattern} at the requested occurrences. If a vector of {\ttfamily Instance} is specified, containing the indices of the specific instances of {\ttfamily Pattern} that must be removed, then only those instances will be removed from the array.  




\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
Generate and return an allocatable array containing the remaining parts of the input array as a sequence after removing the input {\ttfamily Pattern} at the requested occurrences. If a vector of {\ttfamily Instance} is specified, containing the indices of the specific instances of {\ttfamily Pattern} that must be removed, then only those instances will be removed from the array. 


\begin{DoxyParams}[1]{Parameters}
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Array} & \+: The input contiguous array of shape {\ttfamily (\+:)} of either ~\newline

 ~ type {\ttfamily complex} of kind \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceConstants__mod_ac8b456bd9511bc9a52b4a03bda4b72df}{CK32}}, \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceConstants__mod_aa6ea61256fca0b20db0ec2b90755b9f3}{CK64}}, or \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceConstants__mod_ad3873e1ecc5eb3cf3651f72630cae087}{CK128}}, or ~\newline

\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Pattern} & \+: The input contiguous array of shape {\ttfamily (\+:)} or scalar of the same type and kind as the input {\ttfamily Array} containing the pattern that must be removed from the input {\ttfamily Array}. \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em iseq} & \+: The optional external user-\/specified function that takes two input {\bfseries{explicit-\/shape}} arguments of the same type and kind as the input {\ttfamily Array} and possibly, also the length of the arguments as the third argument. It returns a scalar {\ttfamily logical} of default kind \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceConstants__mod_a68ac316f10b57be996670bc7c0abed9d}{LK}} that is {\ttfamily .true.} if all elements of the two input arguments are equivalent (e.\+g., equal) according to the user-\/defined criterion, otherwise, it is {\ttfamily .false.}. If {\ttfamily Pattern} is an array of shape {\ttfamily (\+:)} or an assumed-\/length scalar {\ttfamily character}, then the last argument to {\ttfamily iseq} is the length of the input {\ttfamily Pattern}, preceded by a slice of {\ttfamily Array} and {\ttfamily Pattern} as the first and second arguments, whose lengths are given by the third argument {\ttfamily len\+Pattern}. ~\newline

\end{DoxyCode}
 This user-\/defined equivalence check is extremely useful where a user-\/defined equivalence test other than exact equality or identity is needed, for example, when the array segments should match the input {\ttfamily Pattern} only within a given threshold or, when the case-\/sensitivity in character comparisons do not matter. In such cases, user can define a custom equivalence criterion within the user-\/defined external function {\ttfamily iseq} to achieve the goal. ({\bfseries{optional}}, the default equivalence operator is {\ttfamily .eqv.} if the input {\ttfamily Array} is {\ttfamily logical}, otherwise {\ttfamily ==}). \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em Instance} & \+: The input contiguous array of shape {\ttfamily (\+:)} of type {\ttfamily integer} of default kind \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceConstants__mod_a2bf4d6767c9954d3a495d10ab6b538d6}{IK}}, containing the instances of the input {\ttfamily Pattern} in the input {\ttfamily Array} that should be removed. ~\newline
 Any element of {\ttfamily Instance} that points to an out-\/of-\/scope instance of {\ttfamily Pattern} in the input {\ttfamily Array} will be ignored. ~\newline
 Any element of {\ttfamily Instance} that is negatively valued will be counted from end of the input {\ttfamily Array}. ~\newline
 For example, {\ttfamily Instance = \mbox{[}2,-\/1\mbox{]}} requests removing the second instance of {\ttfamily Pattern} in {\ttfamily Array} from the beginning and removing the first instance of {\ttfamily Pattern} starting from the end of {\ttfamily Array} ({\bfseries{optional}}, the default value corresponds to removing all instances of {\ttfamily Pattern} in {\ttfamily Array}). \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em sorted} & \+: The input {\ttfamily logical} of default kind \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceConstants__mod_a68ac316f10b57be996670bc7c0abed9d}{LK}} indicating whether the elements of the specified input {\ttfamily Instance} are all ascending-\/ordered. This includes the negative elements of {\ttfamily Instance} {\bfseries{after}} they are translated to the corresponding {\bfseries{positive}} instances from the beginning of the input {\ttfamily Array}. Setting {\ttfamily sorted = .true.} will lead faster runtime of the procedure. However, the onus will be strictly on the user to ensure all elements of {\ttfamily Instance} are ascending-\/ordered. This is generally not an easy guarantee to make. Therefore, set {\ttfamily sorted = .true.} {\bfseries{if and only if}} you fully understand the implications. ({\bfseries{optional}}, default = {\ttfamily .false.}. It can be present as input argument {\bfseries{if and only if}} the input argument {\ttfamily Instance} is present). \\
\hline
\mbox{\texttt{ in}}  & {\em unique} & \+: The input {\ttfamily logical} of default kind \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceConstants__mod_a68ac316f10b57be996670bc7c0abed9d}{LK}} indicating whether the elements of the specified input {\ttfamily Instance} are all unique. This includes the negative elements of {\ttfamily Instance} {\bfseries{after}} they are translated to the corresponding {\bfseries{positive}} instances from the beginning of the input {\ttfamily Array}. Setting {\ttfamily unique = .true.} will lead faster runtime of the procedure. However, the onus will be strictly on the user to ensure all elements of {\ttfamily Instance} are unique. This is generally not an easy guarantee to make. Therefore, set {\ttfamily unique = .true.} {\bfseries{if and only if}} you fully understand the implications. ({\bfseries{optional}}, default = {\ttfamily .false.}. It can be present as input argument {\bfseries{if and only if}} the input argument {\ttfamily Instance} is present).\\
\hline
\end{DoxyParams}
\begin{DoxyReturn}{Returns}
{\ttfamily Array\+New} \+: The output allocatable of the same type, kind, and rank as the input {\ttfamily Array} argument containing the remaining parts of the array in sequence after removing the requested (or all) instances of {\ttfamily Pattern}.
\end{DoxyReturn}

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
This procedure is {\ttfamily impure} when the library is compiled with macro {\ttfamily CHECK\+\_\+\+ENABLED=1}. By default, it is {\ttfamily pure} in {\ttfamily release} build and {\ttfamily impure} in {\ttfamily debug} and {\ttfamily testing} builds.

The purity of the procedure breaks when the input external procedure {\ttfamily iseq} is specified as input argument.

Note that in Fortran, trailing blanks are ignored in character comparison, that is, {\ttfamily \char`\"{}\+Fortran\char`\"{} == \char`\"{}\+Fortran \char`\"{}} yields {\ttfamily .true.}.
\end{DoxyWarning}
\begin{DoxyRemark}{Remarks}
The functions under this interface could be slightly slower than the \mbox{\hyperlink{interfaceArrayRemove__mod_1_1remove}{remove}} subroutine implementations due to the extra copy action required upon return from the function. See \mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceArrayRemove__mod}{Array\+Remove\+\_\+mod}} for the relevant benchmarks.
\end{DoxyRemark}

\textcolor{fortran_operator_symbols}{+}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0.}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0}\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{0},\textcolor{fortran_operator_symbols}{ \end{DoxyParagraph}
\begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Test}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{test__test000008}{Test}}]\mbox{\hyperlink{namespaceTest__ArrayRemove__mod}{Test\+\_\+\+Array\+Remove\+\_\+mod}}\end{DoxyRefDesc}


\begin{DoxyRefDesc}{Bug}
\item[\mbox{\hyperlink{bug__bug000006}{Bug}}]The Intel Fortran compiler Classic 2021.\+2.\+0 has a bug for the following interface definition \end{DoxyRefDesc}

\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_comment}{character(len(Array))   , allocatable   :: ArrayNew(:)}}

\end{DoxyCode}
 leading to an {\bfseries{internal compiler error}}. For now, the remedy seems to be to redefine the interface as, 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_comment}{character(:), allocatable   :: ArrayNew(:)}}

\end{DoxyCode}
 and changing the allocation method accordingly in the implementation to, 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{allocate}(\textcolor{fortran_statement}{character}(\textcolor{fortran_function}{len}(Array,\textcolor{fortran_spcifier}{ kind}\textcolor{fortran_operator_symbols}{ = }IK)) :: ArrayNew(lenArrayNew))}

\end{DoxyCode}
 However, this introduces {\ttfamily internal compiler error\+: Segmentation fault} with gfortran versions 10 and 11. Here is a code snippet to regenerate the bug in Intel ifort (uncomment the commented line to reproduce the gfortran bug), 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{module} ExplicitLenResult\_mod}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{implicit none}}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{interface}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_attribute}{        pure} \textcolor{fortran_prefix}{module function }bug(Array) \textcolor{fortran_suffix}{result}(ArrayNew)}
\DoxyCodeLine{            \textcolor{fortran_statement}{character}(\textcolor{fortran_operator_symbols}{*}),\textcolor{fortran_attribute}{ intent(in)},\textcolor{fortran_attribute}{ contiguous}    :: Array(:)}
\DoxyCodeLine{            \textcolor{fortran_statement}{character}(\textcolor{fortran_function}{len}(Array))   ,\textcolor{fortran_attribute}{ allocatable}   :: ArrayNew(:) \textcolor{fortran_comment}{! catastrophic internal error with ifort 2021.2. Fine with gfortran 10.3}}
\DoxyCodeLine{           \textcolor{fortran_comment}{!character(:)            , allocatable   :: ArrayNew(:) ! catastrophic internal error with gfortran 10.3. Fine with ifort 2021.2}}
\DoxyCodeLine{        \textcolor{fortran_statement}{end function}}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{end interface}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{end module }ExplicitLenResult\_mod}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{submodule} (ExplicitLenResult\_mod) Routines\_smod}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{implicit none}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{contains}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{    module procedure} bug}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{       allocate}(ArrayNew,\textcolor{fortran_spcifier}{ source}\textcolor{fortran_operator_symbols}{ = }Array)}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{end procedure}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{end submodule} Routines\_smod}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{program} \mbox{\hyperlink{main_8f90_a8ec2266d83cd6c0b762cbcbc92c0af3d}{main}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{use }ExplicitLenResult\_mod, \textcolor{fortran_statement}{only}: bug}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{character}(\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{2}) :: Array(\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{3})\textcolor{fortran_operator_symbols}{ = }[\textcolor{fortran_string}{"{}AA"{}}, \textcolor{fortran_string}{"{}BB"{}}, \textcolor{fortran_string}{"{}CC"{}}]}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{character}(\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{2}),\textcolor{fortran_attribute}{ allocatable} :: ArrayNew(:)}
\DoxyCodeLine{    ArrayNew\textcolor{fortran_operator_symbols}{ = }bug(Array)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{end program }main}

\end{DoxyCode}
 It turns out that both gfortran and Intel do not tolerate the separation of interface from implementation in the above code snippet. If one duplicates the interface in the implementation submodule, then both compilers compile and run the code with no errors. This is the remedy that is currently used in this \mbox{\hyperlink{interfaceArrayRemove__mod_1_1genRemoved}{gen\+Removed}} generic interface (interface duplication where the bug exists). Here is a workaround example for the bug in the above code snippet, 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{module} ExplicitLenResult\_mod}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{implicit none}}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{interface}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_attribute}{        pure} \textcolor{fortran_prefix}{module function }bug(Array) \textcolor{fortran_suffix}{result}(ArrayNew)}
\DoxyCodeLine{            \textcolor{fortran_statement}{character}(\textcolor{fortran_operator_symbols}{*}),\textcolor{fortran_attribute}{ intent(in)},\textcolor{fortran_attribute}{ contiguous}    :: Array(:)}
\DoxyCodeLine{            \textcolor{fortran_statement}{character}(\textcolor{fortran_function}{len}(Array))   ,\textcolor{fortran_attribute}{ allocatable}   :: ArrayNew(:) \textcolor{fortran_comment}{! catastrophic internal error with ifort 2021.2. Fine with gfortran 10.3}}
\DoxyCodeLine{        \textcolor{fortran_statement}{end function}}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{end interface}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{end module }ExplicitLenResult\_mod}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{submodule} (ExplicitLenResult\_mod) Routines\_smod}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{implicit none}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{contains}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{    module procedure} bug}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{       allocate}(ArrayNew,\textcolor{fortran_spcifier}{ source}\textcolor{fortran_operator_symbols}{ = }Array)}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{end procedure}}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{end submodule} Routines\_smod}
\DoxyCodeLine{}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{program} \mbox{\hyperlink{main_8f90_a8ec2266d83cd6c0b762cbcbc92c0af3d}{main}}}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{use }ExplicitLenResult\_mod, \textcolor{fortran_statement}{only}: bug}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{character}(\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{2}) :: Array(\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{3})\textcolor{fortran_operator_symbols}{ = }[\textcolor{fortran_string}{"{}AA"{}}, \textcolor{fortran_string}{"{}BB"{}}, \textcolor{fortran_string}{"{}CC"{}}]}
\DoxyCodeLine{    \textcolor{fortran_statement}{character}(\textcolor{fortran_numeric_literal}{2}),\textcolor{fortran_attribute}{ allocatable} :: ArrayNew(:)}
\DoxyCodeLine{    ArrayNew\textcolor{fortran_operator_symbols}{ = }bug(Array)}
\DoxyCodeLine{\textcolor{fortran_statement}{end program }main}

\end{DoxyCode}
